тАШрдЕрдирд░реНрдердХрдВ рдЪ рддрджреНрд╡рдЪрдирдореН ’ рдЗрддрд┐ ред рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рд╖реНрдЯреБрддрд┐ рд╢реНрд░реВрдпрддреЗ- рдЖрдЧреНрдиреЗрдпрд╛ рдЧреНрд░рд╣рд╛ рднрд╡рдиреНрддрд┐’ рдЗрддрд┐ ред рддрддреНрд░реИрд╡ рдкреБрдирд░рдкреНрдпрдиреНрдпрджреБрдЪреНрдпрддреЗ-рдЖрдЧреНрдиреЗрдпреАрд╖реБ рд╕реНрддреБрд╡рддреЗ ред рдЖрдЧреНрдиреЗрдпреАрдГ рд╢рдВрд╕рдиреНрддрд┐’ рдЗрддрд┐ ред рддреНрд╡рддреНрдкрдХреНрд╖реЗ рддрджреНрд╡рдЪрдирдордирд░реНрдердХрдВ рд╕реНрдпрд╛рддреН редред рдЪреЛрджрдХрдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрддреЗрд╖реБ рд╕реНрддреЛрддреНрд░рд╢рд╕реНрддреНрд░рдордиреНрддреНрд░реЗрд╖реНрд╡рд╛рдЧреНрдиреЗрдпрдЧреНрд░рд╣рд╛рдиреБрд╕рд╛рд░реЗрдг рджреЗрд╡рддрд╛рдкрджрд╕реНрдп рдКрд╣реЗ рд╕рддрд┐ рдЖрдЧреНрдиреЗрдпрддреНрд╡рд╕рд┐рджреНрдзреЗрдГ ред рдкреНрд░рдзрд╛рдирдХрд░реНрдордкрдХреНрд╖реЗ рддреБ рджреЗрд╡рддрд╛рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢рдирд░реВрдкрд╕реНрд╡рд╛рднрд╛рд╡реЗрди рдКрд╣рд╛рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рддреН рдЖрдЧреНрдиреЗрдпрдордиреНрддреНрд░рд╛рдиреНрддрд░рд╡рд┐рдзрд┐рд╡рдЪрдирдорд░реНрдерд╡рджреНрднрд╡рддрд┐ рее рдкреБрдирд░рдкрд┐ рд╣реЗрддреНрд╡рдиреНрддрд░рдорд╛рд╣—-

Jamison Brereton

2
Va╠Дyu (1тАУ3), Indra and Va╠Дyu (4тАУ6), Mitra and Varun╠гa (7тАУ9)
Madhuchandas Vai┼Ыv─Бmitra
9 verses: g─Бyatr─л, arranged in tr╠еcas
This and the following hymn constitute what is later called the Pra├╝ga┼Ыastra, the тАЬyoke-pole-tip recitation,тАЭ which is the second recited litany in the morning soma pressing. In classical ┼Ыrauta ritual the ┼Ыastra consists of seven sets of three verses or tr╠еcas. In the recitation each triplet of verses is preceded by an introductory nivid, a brief declaration of the deities invoked in the recitation. Recitations typically combine verses from different hymns, or they may require that the form of the R╠еgvedic verses be recast, but in this case the nivids need only be added to produce the recitation. These two hymns, therefore, are already fit for the classical performance of the soma ritual.
As Insler (2002) has shown, the sequence of gods in I.2тАУ3 represents the sequence of gods who receive cups of soma during the soma-pressing day. The rite reflected in the hymns was neither a version of the soma ritual represented in the Family Books of the R╠еgveda nor that of the classical ritual, although it comes fairly close to the latter. Rather, these two hymns represent a transitional period in the develop
ment of the soma rite as it moved toward its classical form.
In the R╠еgvedic rite, V─Бyu was the first of the gods to receive the soma and there fore the first tr╠еca of I.2 is dedicated to him. In the classical rite, the recipients of soma at the Morning Pressing are, for the most part, dual divinities. The first pair is Indra and V─Бyu, to whom our second tr╠еca (vss. 4тАУ6) is dedicated, and the second pair is Mitra and Varuс╣Зa, addressed in our third tr╠еca (vss. 7тАУ9).
In I.3 the first tr╠еca is dedicated to the two A┼Ыvins, who are the third set of dual divinities at the classical Morning Pressing. In the classical rite there are also morn ing offerings to Indra and to the All Gods. Those gods are mentioned in the next two tr╠еcas (Indra, vss. 4тАУ6; the All Gods, vss. 7тАУ9), but at the time of the composition of these hymns, these verses probably refer to the midday and evening rites rather than to the morning offering.
In most of the Family Books of the R╠еgveda, Indra alone is the principal at the Midday Pressing, though especially in Maс╣Зс╕Нala III there is evidence that the Maruts have joined Indra as dedicands, as in the classical rite. The Maruts are not mentioned in our hymn, however, and were probably not a part of the soma rite for which these hymns were composed. Although the R╠еbhus and Indra were the principal recipients of soma at the Third Pressing for most of the R╠еgvedic period, the R╠еbhus are absent from this hymn, indicating that, as also in the classical rite, they had already all but disappeared from the soma rite. Rather, in this hymn and in the classical rite, there is a soma offering to the All Gods in the evening. This association of the All Gods with the Third Pressing must be fairly old, since the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa texts refer to the Third Pressing as vai┼Ыvadevyam тАЬbelonging to the All Gods.тАЭ The last tr╠еca (vss. 10тАУ12) of I.3 is to Sarasvat─л, who does not receive an offering in the Third Pressing at the classical rite and has only a limited presence in the R╠еgveda. However, she likely did receive soma at the Third Pressing in the period of this transitional rite.
For further on this ┼Ыastra and the order of divinities addressed, see the other hymns with this structure, I.23 and II.41, as well as I.139 in part. It is not clear why the ┼Ыastra has been split into two hymns just in this case.
The actual content of the two hymns is quite simple. In I.2 the first two tr╠еcas to V─Бyu and Indra and V─Бyu respectively announce that the soma has been pressed and urge the gods to come to our sacrifice. The tr╠еca to Mitra and Varuс╣Зa is slightly more interesting, in that it mentions the frequently conjoined notions of тАЬinsightтАЭ (dh─л╠Б), тАЬskillтАЭ (da╠Бkс╣гa), and тАЬresolveтАЭ or тАЬpurposeтАЭ (kra╠Бtu), the three elements neces sary to conceive and carry out an action.

Jamison Brereton Notes

V─Бyu, etc. (Pra├╝ga┼Ыastra)

The recipients of the various tс╣Ыcas making up these two rather simple hymns are clearly signalled. All three verses making up the first tс╣Ыca to V─Бyu (vss. 1-3) open with a voc. v─Бyo; the second tс╣Ыca (to Indra and V─Бyu, vss. 4-6) opens with the voc. ├нndrav─Бy┼л, while the next two begin with the famous тАЬV─Бyav Indra┼Ы caтАЭ construction (on which see Jamison 1988). The pattern is varied in the Mitra and Varuс╣Зa tс╣Ыca (7- 9), with the conjoined accusatives mitr├бm and v├бruс╣Зaс╣Г ca opening the first and second p─Бdas of vs. 7, and the dual dvandva mitr─Б╠Бv├бruс╣З─Б(v) in second position in the next two verses, first as a vocative, then as a nominative.

There appears to be some attempt to create bridges between the tс╣Ыcas: verses 3 and 4 both sketch a reversal of the usual ritual model; vss. 6 and 7 both concern our тАШinsightтАЩ (dh─л╠Б).

English translation:

тАЬV─Бyu, your praisers praise you with holy praises having poured out Soma juice, and knowing the (fit) season.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

With ukthas = with ┼Ыastras (hymns of praise recited, not chanted or sung

Jamison Brereton

O V─Бyu, with their hymns the singers sing you hereтАФ
they who have pressed soma, who understand the (ritual) days.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Geldner suggests that jarante here can be ambiguous, belonging not only to тАШsingтАЩ, but also to тАШawakenтАЩ, with identical present stem. This is possible, but only with an intransitive sense of тАШawakenтАЩ: тАЬthe singers awaken / wake up to you,тАЭ since the тАШawakenтАЩ present is only intrans. (see Got┼Н 1987: 150). In any case surely the primary sense is тАШsingтАЩ, given the the etymological figure produced by its grammatical subj. jarit─Б╠Бraс╕е тАШsingersтАЩ.

English translation:

тАЬV─Бyu, your approving speech comes to the giver (of the libation), and to many (others who invite you) to drink of the Soma juice.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Your approving speech: v─Бyu is supposed to say: ‘I will drink the libation’

Jamison Brereton

O V─Бyu, your nourishing stream infusing (the soma) is going along for the pious manтАФ
the broadly spreading (stream) for soma-drinking.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The difficult words dh├йn─Б and prapс╣Ы├▒cat─л╠Бcomplicate the interpretation of this verse. The former, investigated in detail by H.-P. Schmidt (Gd. Nyberg), is now generally interpreted as тАШ(milk)streamтАЩ, rendering GeldnerтАЩs тАШlipтАЩ and RenouтАЩs тАШtongueтАЩ out of date. As for prapс╣Ы├▒cat─л╠Б, the simplex pс╣Ы├▒cat─л╠Бappears in another Pra├╝ga┼Ыastra hymn (I.23.16), modifying waters and referring to the mixing of milk (acc.) with honey (instr.). Given the similarity of context, a direct object referring to a liquid should be supplied.

What is also puzzling here is in what way the тАШstreamтАЩ is V─БyuтАЩs: it should not originate with him, but rather be destined for him, but then why is the тАШpious manтАЩ apparently receiving the benefit of it? As in the next verse, there seems to be a bit of role reversal here, with the gods depicted as providing the ritual benefits rather than receiving them. Presumably the point is that the pious man gets the benefit secondarily, by having pleased the god, but the dative d─Б┼Ы├║с╣гe is striking, esp. as it is apparently parallel grammatically (though it cannot be functionally) to the dat. s├│map─лtaye ending the verse. Although the verse presumably depicts the sacrificerтАЩs offering of soma to V─Бyu to drink, the lexicon and the case usage complicate the message.

Griffith

Vayu, thy penetrating stream goes forth unto the worshipper,
Far-spreading for the Soma draught.

O Vaju, deine Milchkuh naht weit ausgedehnt zum Somatrank Und schenkt dem Frommen reichlich Gut.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬIndra and V─Бyu, these libations are poured out (for you); come hither with food (for us); verily the drops (of the Soma juice) await you both.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

O Indra and V─Бyu, here are the soma-pressings: come near with delight,
for the soma drops are eager for you.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As noted in the comment on the last verse, the ritual model here is shaken up a bit: Indra and V─Бyu are urged to come with pr├бyobhiс╕е, a word generally used of тАШpleasurable offeringsтАЩ that are presented to the gods and to which they come (cf. VIII.60.4 abh├н pr├бy─Бс╣Гsi … gahi). Our translation тАЬwith delight,тАЭ agreeing with most other translators, avoids, and conceals, the problem. The gods should not be bringing pr├бy─Бс╣Гsi. The little disturbance of the ritual model is confined to these two verses in this hymn.

The p─Бda-final position of h├н here is unusual, and I have no explanation for it, esp. as it does not take second position in its clause as is usual.

I.2.7-9: As mentioned in the introduction, this tс╣Ыca contains the trio dh─л╠БтАШinsightтАЩ (vs. 7), kr├бtu- тАШintentionтАЩ (vs. 8), and d├бkс╣гa- тАШskillтАЩ (vs. 9), the three elements necessary to conceive and carry out an action. Their interconnection is emphasized by the fact that all three are in the accusative and each is stationed initial in the last p─Бda of its verse.

The juxtaposition across vss. 8-9 of kr├бtum (beginning 8c) and kav─л╠Б (beginning 9a) may also be meant to evoke the well-established compound kav├нkratu- тАШhaving the will/resolve of a poetтАЩ, тАШhaving a poetтАЩs purposeтАЩ, an occurrence of which is found in the preceding hymn by the same poet (I.1.5).

Griffith

These, Indra-Vayu, have been shed; come for our offered dainties’ sake:
The drops are yearning for you both.

Keith

O Indra and Vayu, these draughts are ready;
Come ye for the libations,
For the drops desire you.

Geldner

Indra und Vayu! Hier sind die gepre├Яten Tr├дnke; kommet mit Freuden, denn die Somas├дfte verlangen nach euch.

Grassmann

Hier, Indra-Vaju, steht der Saft, so kommt zu ihm nach eurer Lust, Die Tropfen sehnen sich nach euch.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬIndra and V─Бyu, abiding in the sacrificial rite, you are aware of these libations; come both (then) quickly hither.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

O V─Бyu and Indra, you take note of the pressings, you two rich in prizewinning mares.
Drive right here at speed.

Griffith

Well do ye mark libations, ye Vayu and Indra, rich in spoil
So come ye swiftly hitherward.

Geldner

O Vaju, Indra, nehmet wahr der Tr├дnke, labungsreiche ihr, So kommet eilig denn herbei.

English translation:

тАЬV─Бyu and Indra, come to the rite of the sacrificer, for thus, men, will completion be speedily (attained) by the ceremony.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

O V─Бyu and Indra, drive right here to the appointed place of the soma-presser,
swiftly and according to our insight right to the point, you superior men.

Griffith

Vayu and Indra, come to what the Soma. presser hath prepared:
Soon, Heroes, thus I make my prayer.

Geldner

Vayu und Indra! Kommet zum Treffort des Somapressenden, alsbald, so recht nach Wunsch, ihr Herren!

Grassmann

O Vaju, Indra, stellt euch ein zum Ort des Somapressers rasch, O M├дnner, recht mit Achtsamkeit.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬI invoke Mitra, of pure vigour, and Varuс╣Зa, the devourer of foes; the joint accomplishers of the act bestowing water (on the earth).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Mitra = the Sun;

Varuс╣Зa = the regent of the waters; both are among the twelve ─Аdityas; Mitra presides over day, Varuс╣Зa presides over night; dhiyam ghс╣Ыt─Бc─лm s─Бdhant─Б: dhi, an act; ghс╣Ыt─Бc─лm, water-shedding

Jamison Brereton

I call upon Mitra of refined skill and Varuс╣Зa, who cares for the stranger, the two who send our ghee-covered insight to its goal.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Here and everywhere else it is found, the word ri┼Ы─Б╠Бdas-, an epithet of various gods, is opaque. There are currently two competing and entirely different interpretations: that of Karl Hoffmann (Aufs. 564 n. 16) as тАШdiscriminating, fastidiousтАЩ (тЖР тАШpicking at foodтАЩ) and Paul ThiemeтАЩs тАШcaring for the strangerтАЩ (Fremdling). See EWA s.v. The contexts are not diagnostic, and it is probably the case that the epithet was no longer understood even as it was being deployed (note that it is almost always p─Бda-final, possibly a sign of formulaic freezing).

Throughout our translation we have followed the Thieme interpretation, but not with any great conviction. One thing in favor of the Thieme interpretation is that the word is regularly applied to one or more of the ─Аdityas (as here), who might be expected to show care for humans in their charge. That it is also regularly used of the less ethically inclined Maruts might give us pause (though these contexts are generally benevolent ones) - except that тАШfastidiousтАЩ is even less a likely quality of the Maruts than тАШcaring for the strangerтАЩ.

Griffith

Mitra, of holy strength, I call, and foe-destroying Varuna,
Who make the oil-fed rite complete.

Geldner

Ich rufe den Mitra von lauterer Wirkenskraft und Varuna, den herrenstolzen, die beide das gesalbte Gedicht gelingen lassen.

Grassmann

Den heilgen Mitra rufe ich, den Feindverzehrer Varuna, Die Opfer segnen und Gebet:

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬMitra and Varuс╣Зa, augmenters of water, dispensers of water, you connect this perfect rite with its true (reward).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

с╣Ъt─Бvс╣Ыdhau: с╣Ыta = tue or truth; it also signifies water and sacrifice].

Jamison Brereton

By truthтАФ o Mitra and Varuс╣Зa, strong through truth, touching truthтАФ you have attained your lofty purpose.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The unaccented voc. с╣Ыt─Бvс╣Ыdh─Бv opening the 2nd p─Бda has been thus transmitted, though we would expect *с╣Ы╠Бt─Бvс╣Ыdh─Бv. In fact there is a striking string of 13 unaccented syllables in this hemistich, starting after the first word of the vs., с╣Ыt├йna (14, counting -na). See Oldenberg, who has no good explanation for the lack of accent on the first word of the 2nd p─Бda, though he considers it an old error. It cannot be simply a peculiarity of this hymn, because I.3.1b (forming part of the Pra├╝ga┼Ыastra sequence with I.2, as discussed in the published introduction.) opens with an initially accented voc. dr├бvatp─Бс╣З─л (to the stem drav├бtp─Бс╣Зi-).

Griffith

Mitra and Varuna, through Law, lovers and cherishers of Law,
Have ye obtained your might power.

Geldner

Durch die Wahrheit habt ihr, Mitra und Varuna, ihr Wahrheitsmehrer, Wahrheits-pfleger, hohe Einsicht erlangt.

Grassmann

Durch Recht, o Mitra-Varuna, die Recht ihr liebt und Recht beschirmt, Habt hohe Weisheit ihr erlangt.

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдХрд╡реА) рдХреНрд░рд╛рдиреНрддрджрд░реНрд╢рдиреМ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╡реНрдпрд╡рд╣рд╛рд░рджрд░реНрд╢рдирд╣реЗрддреВред рдХрд╡рд┐рдГ рдХреНрд░рд╛рдиреНрддрджрд░реНрд╢рдиреЛ рднрд╡рддрд┐ рдХрд╡рддреЗрд░реНрд╡рд╛ред (рдирд┐рд░реБрежрезреи.резрей) рдПрддрдиреНрдирд┐рд░реБрдХреНрддрд╛рднрд┐рдкреНрд░рд╛рдпреЗрдг рдХрд╡рд┐рд╢рдмреНрджреЗрди рд╕реБрдЦрд╕рд╛рдзрдХреМ рдорд┐рддреНрд░рд╛рд╡рд░реБрдгреМ рдЧреГрд╣реНрдпреЗрддреЗред (рдирдГ) рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдХрдореН (рдорд┐рддреНрд░рд╛рд╡рд░реБрдгреМ) рдкреВрд░реНрд╡реЛрдХреНрддреМ (рддреБрд╡рд┐рдЬрд╛рддреМ) рдмрд╣реБрднреНрдпрдГ рдХрд╛рд░рдгреЗрднреНрдп рдЙрддреНрдкрдиреНрдиреМ рдмрд╣реБрд╖реБ рд╡рд╛ рдкреНрд░рд╕рд┐рджреНрдзреМред рддреБрд╡реАрддрд┐ рдмрд╣реБрдирд╛рдорд╕реБ рдкрдард┐рддрдореНред (рдирд┐рдШрдВрежрей.рез) (рдЙрд░реБрдХреНрд╖рдпрд╛) рдмрд╣реБрд╖реБ рдЬрдЧрддреНрдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдереЗрд╖реБ рдХреНрд╖рдпреЛ рдирд┐рд╡рд╛рд╕реЛ рдпрдпреЛрд╕реНрддреМред рдЕрддреНрд░ рд╕реБрдкрд╛рдВ рд╕реБрд▓реБрдЧрд┐рддреНрдпрд╛рдХрд╛рд░рдГред рдЙрд░реНрд╡рд┐рддрд┐ рдмрд╣реБрдирд╛рдорд╕реБ рдкрдард┐рддрдореНред (рдирд┐рдШрдВрежрей.рез) тАШрдХреНрд╖рд┐ рдирд┐рд╡рд╛рд╕рдЧрддреНрдпреЛрдГтАЩ рдЕрд╕реНрдп рдзрд╛рддреЛрд░рдзрд┐рдХрд░рдгрд╛рд░реНрдердГ рдХреНрд╖рдпрд╢рдмреНрджрдГред (рджрдХреНрд╖рдореН) рдмрд▓рдореН (рджрдзрд╛рддреЗ) рдзрд░рддрдГ (рдЕрдкрд╕рдореН) рдХрд░реНрдоред рдЕрдк рдЗрддрд┐ рдХрд░реНрдордирд╛рдорд╕реБ рдкрдард┐рддрдореНред (рдирд┐рд░реБрежреи.рез) рд╡реНрдпрддреНрдпрдпреЛ рдмрд╣реБрд▓рдорд┐рддрд┐ рд▓рд┐рдЩреНрдЧрд╡реНрдпрддреНрдпрдпрдГред рдЗрджрдордкрд┐ рд╕рд╛рдпрдгрд╛рдЪрд╛рд░реНрдпреНрдпреЗрдг рди рдмреБрджреНрдзрдореНреерепрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдорд╛рдгреНрдбрд╕реНрдерд╛рднреНрдпрд╛рдВ рдмрд▓рдХрд░реНрдордирд┐рдорд┐рддреНрддрд╛рднреНрдпрд╛рдореЗрддрд╛рднреНрдпрд╛рдВ рд╕рд░реНрд╡реЗрд╖рд╛рдВ рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдирд╛рдВ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рдЪреЗрд╖реНрдЯрд╛рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрдпреЛрдГ рдкреБрд╖реНрдЯрд┐рдзрд╛рд░рдгреЗ рднрд╡рдд рдЗрддрд┐реерепрее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдорд╛рдВрдбрд╛рдд рдЕрд╕рдгрд╛рд░реЗ рдмрд▓ рд╡ рдХрд░реНрдорд╛рдирд┐рдорд┐рддреНрдд рдкреВрд░реНрд╡реЛрдХреНрдд рдЬреЗ рдорд┐рддреНрд░ рд╡ рд╡рд░реБрдг рдЖрд╣реЗрдд, рддреНрдпрд╛рдВрдЪреНрдпрд╛рдХрдбреВрди рдХреНрд░рд┐рдпрд╛ рд╡ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛ рдпрд╛рдВрдЪреА рдкреБрд╖реНрдЯреА рд╡ рдзрд╛рд░рдгрд╛ рд╣реЛрддреЗ. рее реп рее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рдкрд╛рджрдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреА

рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдгреА: рдпрд╛ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдЪрд╛ рд╕рд╛рдпрдгрд╛рдЪрд╛рд░реНрдп рдЗрддреНрдпрд╛рджреА рд╡ рд╡рд┐рд▓реНрд╕рди рдЗрддреНрдпрд╛рджреА рдпреБрд░реЛрдк рджреЗрд╢рд╡рд╛рд╕реА рд▓реЛрдХрд╛рдВрдиреА рд╡реЗрдЧрд│рд╛рдЪ рдЕрд░реНрде рд╕рд╛рдВрдЧрд┐рддрд▓реЗрд▓рд╛ рдЖрд╣реЗ.
